  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6dec1dd3-5b7b-4655-b6db-85d55dc7aacc'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div id="review_1399092196" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1399092196" />
    <a title="Yvette" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9140034-yvette"><img alt="Yvette" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422016374p2/9140034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1399092196?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yvette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yvette" href="/user/show/9140034-yvette">Yvette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9140034-yvette?shelf=my-library">my-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9140034-yvette?shelf=owned-poetry">owned-poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1399092196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3103126135727816057">If you are looking for elegant poetry with wonderful imagery and words put together in a beautiful way you've never thought of before, skip this book.<br/><br/>This book reminds me of Lang Leav, whose work I do not enjoy. It took me a year to finish this book, which is a pity because I remember being really excited for it at first.<br/><br/>When I read poetry, I expect to feel something. Of course, poetry doesn't have to make literal sense, but I expect the meaning of the poem to be <i>felt</i>.<br/><br/>In this book, everything is</span>
  <span id="freeText3103126135727816057" style="display:none">If you are looking for elegant poetry with wonderful imagery and words put together in a beautiful way you've never thought of before, skip this book.<br /><br />This book reminds me of Lang Leav, whose work I do not enjoy. It took me a year to finish this book, which is a pity because I remember being really excited for it at first.<br /><br />When I read poetry, I expect to feel something. Of course, poetry doesn't have to make literal sense, but I expect the meaning of the poem to be <i>felt</i>.<br /><br />In this book, everything is said, and nothing is shown. You are told how to feel, and why you are feeling this way. The words are flat and literal and boring. For example:<br /><br /><blockquote><b>The Whole World Is Watching</b><br /><br />You're younger than you'll be tomorrow. You've never been closer to the day you die. Go. Now.<br /><br /><b>The Person Happiness Became</b><br /><br />So if you love me but you don't need me, you don't love me.</blockquote><br /><br />Most of the book is filled with sappy lines like those. Yes, there are a few lines I loved such as<br /><br /><blockquote>I am made of ghost notes, from songs you never heard.</blockquote><br /><br />There are a number of pieces that would have worked very well if only the author trusted the reader to infer and make their own meaning more. A pity; I so wanted to like this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3103126135727816057" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2228139607" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2228139607" />
    <a title="Ronak Gajjar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70806774-ronak-gajjar"><img alt="Ronak Gajjar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525528784p2/70806774.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2228139607?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronak Gajjar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronak Gajjar" href="/user/show/70806774-ronak-gajjar">Ronak Gajjar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70806774-ronak-gajjar?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70806774-ronak-gajjar?shelf=stand-alones">stand-alones</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70806774-ronak-gajjar?shelf=read-before-and-in-2017">read-before-and-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70806774-ronak-gajjar?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2228139607" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14156111833356973834">The type of poetry: <i>
  <b>Free Verse</b>
</i> <br/><b>REPEATED! REPEATED! REPEATED! REPEATED! REPEATED! REPEATED! REPEATED! </b><br/>And still:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514445352ra/24775347.gif' width='475' height='350' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>The <b>Title</b> + <b>Canto</b> concept, merged along with volume I. But, <br/><i> Don’t you worry. Everything will be easier when they can just plug a fountain pen nib straight into your heart.</i><br/>This one was divided among substantial titles: <b>On love found</b>, <b>On being in love</b>, <b>On love lost</b>, <b>On despair</b>, <b>On hope</b>, <b>On living</b> and <b>On dying</b>. Well, titles themselves justify the same hierarchical order followed in vo</span>
  <span id="freeText14156111833356973834" style="display:none">The type of poetry: <i>
  <b>Free Verse</b>
</i> <br><b>REPEATED! REPEATED! REPEATED! REPEATED! REPEATED! REPEATED! REPEATED! </b><br>And still:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514445352ra/24775347.gif" width="475" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The <b>Title</b> + <b>Canto</b> concept, merged along with volume I. But, <br><i> Don’t you worry. Everything will be easier when they can just plug a fountain pen nib straight into your heart.</i><br>This one was divided among substantial titles: <b>On love found</b>, <b>On being in love</b>, <b>On love lost</b>, <b>On despair</b>, <b>On hope</b>, <b>On living</b> and <b>On dying</b>. Well, titles themselves justify the same hierarchical order followed in volume I. <br>The constant paradox between quotations is pleasantly bizarre. One second you fight with your conscience, next second you pamper it, third you end it up crying, very next a splintered smile! Such as:<br><i>I’m not scared of never meeting you. I’m scared of having met you and let you go.</i><br>You feel an unruly nervousness. <br><i>Wish you were here. Wish I was there. Wish it was different. Wish wishes came true. I’d wish you back.</i> <br>And you are suddenly in Bazaar of wishes. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514445352ra/24775346.gif" width="500" height="264" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> Rather than being so abstract, the verses are simple yet precisely adequate to convey the meaning. I will recommend again this one to everyone. <br>Let me end it with my favorite quote:<br><i>
  <b> You’re just another story. I can’t tell anymore. <b></b></b>
</i> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514451968ra/24776384.gif" width="500" height="197" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>P.S.: I Am NOT restraining myself from showering this review with cheesy gifs. It made me feel “Love” isn’t, after all, an alien feeling.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14156111833356973834" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1501112631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer171105831700066482">I wanted to like it, I did. There were some really wonderful pieces that might even stay with me for a while. But they were few and far between in a book of poetry that was all tell and no show. It mostly felt repetitive and too obvious. <br/><br/>I think many of the poems would have been better as a line in a longer poem than they were attempting to stand alone. Some of them I genuinely thought I had already read earlier in the work. The poet uses a lot of parallel structures and repetition of themes, bu</span>
  <span id="freeText171105831700066482" style="display:none">I wanted to like it, I did. There were some really wonderful pieces that might even stay with me for a while. But they were few and far between in a book of poetry that was all tell and no show. It mostly felt repetitive and too obvious. <br /><br />I think many of the poems would have been better as a line in a longer poem than they were attempting to stand alone. Some of them I genuinely thought I had already read earlier in the work. The poet uses a lot of parallel structures and repetition of themes, but it doesn't come off as intentional. As a whole work it just felt like it could have used some major editing.</span>

I struggled a bit with this book. I just found all the poems to be a bit...<i>nothing</i>. They were all very <b>surface level</b> and although they seemed nice when I first read them I found I forgot them immediately after putting the book down. <i>There wasn't any depth</i> to them in my opinion and it just seemed like they were a bit cliche, <b>written in a formulaic way to appeal to a wide aud</b></span>
  <span id="freeText3667833387206079745" style="display:none"><b>DNF 52 pages in.</b><br /><br />I bought this book when it was quite cheap and thought I would like it because, in general, I enjoy poetry. I struggled a bit with this book. I just found all the poems to be a bit...<i>nothing</i>. They were all very <b>surface level</b> and although they seemed nice when I first read them I found I forgot them immediately after putting the book down. <i>There wasn't any depth</i> to them in my opinion and it just seemed like they were a bit cliche, <b>written in a formulaic way to appeal to a wide audience.</b> Not the book for me but others might still enjoy it.</span>

    <a title="Eliza Barry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54015299-eliza-barry"><img alt="Eliza Barry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458261627p2/54015299.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1582932091?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1582932091" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9793916534260531165">This collection borders on the absurd. Its admirers claim there is something for everyone in here. And then you come across something along the lines of, "This is only for you, the words, blah, blah, blah. Only you get it, blah, blah, blah...", which excludes as a rule. <br/><br/>I'm extremely disenchanted with this whole poetry-as-a-gimmick shtick these poets and publishers have sunk to in order to sell poetry. This collection is no different than the depressingly generic, high school level, cafe-latte-p</span>
  <span id="freeText9793916534260531165" style="display:none">This collection borders on the absurd. Its admirers claim there is something for everyone in here. And then you come across something along the lines of, "This is only for you, the words, blah, blah, blah. Only you get it, blah, blah, blah...", which excludes as a rule. <br /><br />I'm extremely disenchanted with this whole poetry-as-a-gimmick shtick these poets and publishers have sunk to in order to sell poetry. This collection is no different than the depressingly generic, high school level, cafe-latte-poetry Lang Leav is a perpetrator of. <br /><br />Conclusion: nothing worthwhile to see here, folks. Move along. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16276063783770433936">I think I may have judged this book too early to start with. But as I kept reading I figured out the greater purpose of this book. Each and every quote in this book can be applied to anyone's life however they wish. Each and every one of the quotes were so beautiful, I just wanted to tab every single page, except that it was borrowed.</span>

  <span id="freeText1732390410373011444" style="display:none">*4.5*<br /><br />This collection of poems was sitting on my shelf for so long that I just had to pick it out in January<br />I absolutely loved it. I have to admit it, yeah, mea culpa, I saw Harry Styles reading this and I bought the book cause Harry Styles is the purest thing on Earth and we should all agree to that.<br />I'll write a nonfiction book about it someday. Okay, well, let's go back to the book.<br />I like this kind of poetry. It is very direct, and it goes straight through the heart. I am, right now, not in a good place concerning my mental health, and some of these poems really helpmed me some days. The last part was kind of depressing, personally I would have made the choice to end the collection with poems about life rather than death, but I can totally see why the author did that and I respect that a lot. The photography was also amazing, so shoutout to that.<br />Great read all in all, I would totally recommend it if you like "modern poetry" or poetry that goes straight to your heart.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Haidy Abouelnasr" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Haidy Abouelnasr" href="/user/show/14824377-haidy-abouelnasr">Haidy Abouelnasr</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3185071982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16811837868375813208"><br/>I took my time reading this book, because sometimes I couldn’t help but re-read the same page over and over again, trying, but failing, to get over how lovely the writing is; how the author managed to so beautifully and carefully put your thoughts and feelings into words and make them art; how in those times, it really did feel like this book was written just for you. <br/><br/>There were so many entries I loved and so many I’ve highlighted, but my absolute favorite was:<br/><br/><br/><i> The Importance of Correctly Number</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16811837868375813208" style="display:none"><br />I took my time reading this book, because sometimes I couldn’t help but re-read the same page over and over again, trying, but failing, to get over how lovely the writing is; how the author managed to so beautifully and carefully put your thoughts and feelings into words and make them art; how in those times, it really did feel like this book was written just for you. <br /><br />There were so many entries I loved and so many I’ve highlighted, but my absolute favorite was:<br /><br /><br /><i> The Importance of Correctly Numbering Things<br /><br />“There are more grains of sand in the soles of your shoes than you will be given winters to dream or summers to make those dreams real.<br /><br />And there are more stars in the sky than there are grains of sand on Earth.<br /><br />We live in a universe so big that a dying star, in the greater scheme of things, is as significant as spilled milk or an unkissed kiss. In an infinite amount of time, everything that can be forgotten, will be forgotten.<br /><br />In infinity, spilled milk and dying stars matter the same.<br /><br />And if you're just someone brushing your teeth late at night or you're a planet breathing your last breath as you disappear into a black hole, everything you do matters just the same. Every breath you take is as important or unimportant as the sun in the sky or the moon in the night.<br /><br />Scratching your ear, is a kind of miracle, depending on how you look at it.” </i><br /><br /><br />Although I’ve been reading this for over a month, I was still surprised when I reached the end and flipped the last page, I love books that make me feel that way. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1883386022" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1883386022" />
    <a title="Jenb16" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17885015-jenb16"><img alt="Jenb16" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587456778p2/17885015.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1883386022?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenb16" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenb16" href="/user/show/17885015-jenb16">Jenb16</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1883386022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17082913010119403033">I absolutely love poetry and have read so much of it that this book seemed exactly like something up my alley. It was leant to me by a friend of mine who wanted my opinion. This definitely started out on a weak and cheesy note. This book of poetry is split into various sections: On Love Found, On Being in Love, On Love Lost, On Despair, On Hope, On Living, On dying. The love poetry in the beginning was too cliche for me and felt very overdone. This book really turned around for me when I hit the</span>
  <span id="freeText17082913010119403033" style="display:none">I absolutely love poetry and have read so much of it that this book seemed exactly like something up my alley. It was leant to me by a friend of mine who wanted my opinion. This definitely started out on a weak and cheesy note. This book of poetry is split into various sections: On Love Found, On Being in Love, On Love Lost, On Despair, On Hope, On Living, On dying. The love poetry in the beginning was too cliche for me and felt very overdone. This book really turned around for me when I hit the part "On Hope", which in my opinion was the strongest and most beautiful section of the book. I enjoyed "On Living" and "On Dying" as well. I felt that the thoughts and sheer beauty of the words in these sections warranted this book a 4 rating. I think it really deserves a 3.5 but I gave it a 4 for some of the poems that moved me in this work. Overall, I would recommend this book for the poetry lover or anyone who enjoys words that move them. I recommend reading this in fragments, bits and pieces at a time. I also recommend making a nice warm tea or coffee and lighting a few candles! </span>
  <a data-text-id="17082913010119403033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer805802979" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1528653422957487811">I've been following I Wrote This For You since 2007, when it was just a blog. When the first book came out, I was sad to see some of the pieces I'd loved so much (from the blog) not in it. I appreciate this book because it's a collection of everything. Some of mu favorites that had been bookmarked online are in the first few pages. That being said, I am not a fan of the layout only because I feel like there is too much on each page.   <span id="freeText1528653422957487811" style="display:none">I've been following I Wrote This For You since 2007, when it was just a blog. When the first book came out, I was sad to see some of the pieces I'd loved so much (from the blog) not in it. I appreciate this book because it's a collection of everything. Some of mu favorites that had been bookmarked online are in the first few pages. That being said, I am not a fan of the layout only because I feel like there is too much on each page. Maybe this was the only way to fit everything in? This is a personal distraction. What I enjoyed about the first book was the space. Another qualm I have with this is the repetition. I enjoy it to a certain extent, but it feels like a lot of pieces could have been grouped together because of such similarity in the themes and subject matter. This is also a personal distraction.<br /><br />I will always be a fan of Iain Thomas, and I wrote this for you. The writing is simple and beautiful. All in all, this is a wonderful collection. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1528653422957487811" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13997768453650574548">One of my all-time favourite collections. I discovered this book around 4 years ago in the midst of a crippling depressive episode while wandering around a bookstore in the sweatpants I'd been wearing for the 5th consecutive day in a row. It was the sole copy in the store and the cover read 'I wrote this for you and only you. Everyone else who reads it, doesn't get it. They might think they get it, but they don't. This is the sign you've been looking for. You were meant to read these words.' Whi</span>
  <span id="freeText13997768453650574548" style="display:none">One of my all-time favourite collections. I discovered this book around 4 years ago in the midst of a crippling depressive episode while wandering around a bookstore in the sweatpants I'd been wearing for the 5th consecutive day in a row. It was the sole copy in the store and the cover read 'I wrote this for you and only you. Everyone else who reads it, doesn't get it. They might think they get it, but they don't. This is the sign you've been looking for. You were meant to read these words.' While it seems now like the cheesiest thing ever, at the time it truly felt like a sign. To this day, I treasure this book. It is everything it means to be human. It is nostalgic, reassuring and honest. It has provided company and comfort to me in the times when I've felt truly alone. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6860128.Iain_S__Thomas" title="Iain S. Thomas" rel="nofollow noopener">Iain S. Thomas</a>, I found this, thank you.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1444443421&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1444443421" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13408897694652769724">This is the kind of writing that has the ability to rip out your heart and mend it again. It is beautifully written and provides a deeply connected experience between writer and reader. I'll read this a million times and never get sick of it.<br/><br/>I'm so happy I've had the chance to be exposed to such amazing words.<br/><br/>My absolute favourite section was: <br/><br/>“You know I just wouldn’t be human if I didn’t try and hold your hand as it disintegrated from the light of a thousand suns somewhere above Hiroshima. Or </span>
  <span id="freeText13408897694652769724" style="display:none">This is the kind of writing that has the ability to rip out your heart and mend it again. It is beautifully written and provides a deeply connected experience between writer and reader. I'll read this a million times and never get sick of it.<br /><br />I'm so happy I've had the chance to be exposed to such amazing words.<br /><br />My absolute favourite section was: <br /><br />“You know I just wouldn’t be human if I didn’t try and hold your hand as it disintegrated from the light of a thousand suns somewhere above Hiroshima. Or kiss the tears from your cheeks in Iraq, like the sweat from your brow in Zimbabwe. It isn’t in me not to try and lift the rubble crushing you in Gaza or hide you in Rwanda. Like a last hug in a building in New York or the water we shared in Afghanistan. More than the blood we mixed in Flanders or the sandy beach we trod in Normandy. Longer than the fires burned in Dresden or Soweto. I won’t let go of your hand.”<br /><br />Excerpt From: pleasefindthis. “I Wrote This For You.” </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2056674516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12650127846828828010">Those who know me know that I am not a poetry person. At all. I do not feel drawn by most poems and it is always hard for me to feel what poets expect its readers to feel: a connection.<br/><br/>But I decided to give it a try. In all honesty, it didn’t disappoint. I can’t say it is one of my favorite books, but there sure were certain poems or certain quotes that found it’s way to my heart.<br/><br/>This is a little (well, more than 500 pages is not that little) book that reunites a whole set of poetry. It talks ab</span>
  <span id="freeText12650127846828828010" style="display:none">Those who know me know that I am not a poetry person. At all. I do not feel drawn by most poems and it is always hard for me to feel what poets expect its readers to feel: a connection.<br /><br />But I decided to give it a try. In all honesty, it didn’t disappoint. I can’t say it is one of my favorite books, but there sure were certain poems or certain quotes that found it’s way to my heart.<br /><br />This is a little (well, more than 500 pages is not that little) book that reunites a whole set of poetry. It talks about love, loss, grief, death and survival. It also takes you on a self-acceptance, self-esteem and search for happiness journey that, if not all, most people can relate to.</span>

We have all experienced the emotions that love, loss, rejection, and even contentment can bring and this book does an amazing job of bringing those emotions to light. Ultimately, I think the greatest thing I can take from this read is that I am not alone, nor will I ever be, when it comes to feeling every feeling that my experiences allow.</span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_25330489'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25330489-memories"><img alt="Memories" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1459143456l/25330489._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6P+oGnAPw5Iuy2ANBBv7FGkDqXqBMH8cSAvi//vhM8kLIoZbpbDz6NV+7KcR+etRWOFkIT7UfcUai911+xUh7A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ss1fAHiw4icCE2xcsBwldv+DjvasMbMJ4jJP4eufvAepEHFBrQ/SXfmm4Pal/jUzzmFDrRPVsdCwsnBr62uuIg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

There is no Table of Contents. Instead, there is a \"Track List,\" making it easy to refer to them to your friends with a, \"Hey d<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText2568274497505366535\" style=\"display:none\">In Alicia Cook\'s second poetic effort, designed in the style of an old mixtape, she sets her thoughts to a nostalgic tune. There is no Table of Contents. Instead, there is a &quot;Track List,&quot; making it easy to refer to them to your friends with a, &quot;Hey did you read track seven?!&quot; There are no chapters. Instead, the book is divided into two parts, or as one would say in the 90\'s, two &quot;sides.&quot; Side A holds poetry that touches on all aspects of the human condition like life, death, love, moving on, evolving, growing up, hometowns, family dynamic, life after trauma, and make-ups and breakups. Side B holds the &quot;remixes&quot; of these poems, in the form of blackout poetry, also known as &quot;found poetry.&quot; Side B gives the material a fresh twist by creating new poetry out of Side A. There is also a very special surprise at the end of each track. \n\nAlicia decided to self publish this effort after leaving her publishing house. She views this book as her &quot;independence&quot; and official separation from that venture. She also drew the front and back cover herself. \n\nAlicia is a contributing writer for many blogs and news outlets, including the Huffington Post and multiple Gannett Publications. She writes regularly on drug addiction and how it directly affects families. Because of this, she has chosen to donate 100% of royalties to the Willow Tree Center in New Jersey. www.willowtree.org. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13702894124227124987">pleasefindthis (the pen name of Iain S. Thomas) is best known for the I Wrote This For You project, which he began in 2007 as a blog with photographer, Jon Ellis. The project was published as a book in December of 2011 and appears on bestseller lists weekly. <br/><br/>He lives in Cape Town, South Africa and shares his home with his wife, daughter and various animals. </span>

I set out to find you a long time ago and today, I\'m so glad I finally have. Thank you for reading these words.\n\n***\n\nI Wrote This For You is a collaborative photography and prose project. (Almost) every day, the photographer sends the writer a new photograph from wherever he is in the world. The writer creates a poem or short piece of prose inspired by the photograph and focused on whoever might be reading the work, or &quot;you.&quot; The writer and the photographer have never met.  \n\nI Wrote This For You: 2007-2017 is a collection of the best poetry and photography from the first 10 years of the best-selling project. It contains new work, old work, work that\'s never been seen before and a selection of fan-made work inspired by the project. With hundreds of thousands of copies sold, millions of interactions and spanning three existing books, I Wrote This For You has forged a remarkable relationship to its readers over the first 10
